<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_117cd77b-f21f-425f-ac30-975adbf49bd7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7569419431576432215">From the author of Catherine, Called Birdy comes another spellbinding novel set in medieval England. The girl known only as Brat has no family, no home, and no future until she meets Jane the Midwife and becomes her apprentice. As she helps the sharp-tempered Jane deliver babies, Brat--who renames herself Alyce--gains knowledge, confidence, and the courage to want somethin</span>
  <span id="freeText7569419431576432215" style="display:none">From the author of Catherine, Called Birdy comes another spellbinding novel set in medieval England. The girl known only as Brat has no family, no home, and no future until she meets Jane the Midwife and becomes her apprentice. As she helps the sharp-tempered Jane deliver babies, Brat--who renames herself Alyce--gains knowledge, confidence, and the courage to want something from life: "A full belly, a contented heart, and a place in this world." Medieval village life makes a lively backdrop for the funny, poignant story of how Alyce gets what she wants. A concluding note discusses midwifery past and present. A Newbery Medal book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7569419431576432215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_13333393').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_13333393').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_13333393').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script></div>

  <span id="freeText3830475812322766982" style="display:none">I read <b>Catherine Called Birdy</b>, a Newbery Honor Book, about ten years ago, and while it was interesting it wasnâ€™t quite captivating enough for me to want to read anything else by Karen Cushman. Still, when <b>The Midwifeâ€™s Apprentice</b> showed up on Paperback Swap, I figured Iâ€™d give it a try.<br /><br />A Newbery Medal book, The Midwifeâ€™s Apprentice tells the story of a girl with no home, no parents, and no name. One frosty night, she find warmth sleeping in a dung heap. The next morning, Jane Sharp, the village midwife, discovers the girl, who becomes the midwifeâ€™s apprentice. The girl works long, and hard, beyond the point of survival to a place where she thinks and learns and ponders and chooses a name for herself. Her only friend is Purr, a cat she rescues from being drowned by the same boys who torment the girl apprentice. Eventually, she is challenged to deliver a baby in the midwifeâ€™s absence, and her future begins to both unroll and unravel.<br /><br />Karen Cushman has graduate degrees in Human Behavior and Msum Studies. She has a long-standing interest in history. She says, "I grew tired of hearing about kings, princes, generals, and presidents. I wanted to know what life was like for ordinary young people in other times."<br /><br />This book showed off Cushmanâ€™s strengths to their full advantage. Her writing is sure-handed, with lots of showing and not too much telling. She fully brings the reader into a medieval village without overusing words and explanations. The story of <b>The Midwife's Apprentice</b> incorporates realism without fatalism, spirit without warrior-heroics, and a truly empowered character whom readers will love.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16817614373563478528">The midwife finds Brat asleep in a dung heap. She says she will work for food, so the midwife takes her on, having her do the housekeeping and herb-gathering and renames Brat, Beetle. Beetle is not allowed to assist when the midwife delivers a baby, but she watches from the windows and learns the midwifeâ€™s skills.<br/><br/>One day, she gets to go to the fair to buy things for the midwife. There, she decides that she needs a real name, a proper name, and starts calling herself Alyce. One day, in the middle</span>
  <span id="freeText16817614373563478528" style="display:none">The midwife finds Brat asleep in a dung heap. She says she will work for food, so the midwife takes her on, having her do the housekeeping and herb-gathering and renames Brat, Beetle. Beetle is not allowed to assist when the midwife delivers a baby, but she watches from the windows and learns the midwifeâ€™s skills.<br /><br />One day, she gets to go to the fair to buy things for the midwife. There, she decides that she needs a real name, a proper name, and starts calling herself Alyce. One day, in the middle of a difficult birth, the midwife gets called away and leaves Alyce in charge. No one expected the baby to be delivered alive, but Alyce talks the mother through the process and the baby survives.<br /><br />After that, people start coming to Alyce more than the midwife, but when Alyce needs to call the midwife for help during a difficult birth, she sees herself as a failure and runs away, leaving the life she had built for herself.<br /><br />This is a great book for an older child about making your place in the world. It's a Newberry winner and Cushman's attention to historical detail is superb. It's a short, little book, but it's meaty and packs a lot of punch.</span>

<div id="review_62046390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62046390" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62046390?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult">kids-and-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=historic-fiction">historic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62046390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3985096413371521120">I really liked Karen Cushman's books as a kid, and I think one of the big reasons for this (aside from the fact that, although two of her books take place in the Middle Ages, <i>neither</i> protagonist is a princess! *gasp*), is that she never sugar-coats the history. Take <i>The Midwife's Apprentice</i>, which is about a homeless, nameless orphan girl who gets a job as...guess. No, go on, guess.<br/>Delivering babies in the Middle Ages was not only life-threatening and painful, it was <i>gross</i>. I remember reading th</span>
  <span id="freeText3985096413371521120" style="display:none">I really liked Karen Cushman's books as a kid, and I think one of the big reasons for this (aside from the fact that, although two of her books take place in the Middle Ages, <i>neither</i> protagonist is a princess! *gasp*), is that she never sugar-coats the history. Take <i>The Midwife's Apprentice</i>, which is about a homeless, nameless orphan girl who gets a job as...guess. No, go on, guess.<br />Delivering babies in the Middle Ages was not only life-threatening and painful, it was <i>gross</i>. I remember reading this as an impressionable eleven-year-old and deciding that hospitals were pretty much the greatest things ever. And painkillers. And competent doctors who don't rely on the powah of Jesus to help a mother deliver her baby in a time when having a Caesarian guaranteed a slow, painful death. One particularly shocking thing to me was the midwife's method of coaxing a baby out of the womb: she would stick her head between the mother's legs and bellow into the birth canal, "Child, come forth! Christ calls you to the light!" <br /><br />Did I mention how awesome hospitals are? </span>
  <a data-text-id="3985096413371521120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_674995637" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674995637" />
    <a title="Connie  Kuntz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1664750-connie-kuntz"><img alt="Connie  Kuntz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463878527p2/1664750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674995637?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Connie  Kuntz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Connie  Kuntz" href="/user/show/1664750-connie-kuntz">Connie  Kuntz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674995637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4212920519160815387">There will always be a part of me that wishes I was a midwife, so I totally loved this book. The kids did, too, although I am not sure any one of them aspires to midwifery.<br/><br/>The midwife herself is a bully, but Karen Cushman provided just enough detail about her so that the kids and I could not completely despise her. For example, the midwife herself gave birth numerous times, but her babies all died. The midwife also, in spite of being coarse and arrogant, is wise, and she mentions as-a-matter-of-</span>
  <span id="freeText4212920519160815387" style="display:none">There will always be a part of me that wishes I was a midwife, so I totally loved this book. The kids did, too, although I am not sure any one of them aspires to midwifery.<br /><br />The midwife herself is a bully, but Karen Cushman provided just enough detail about her so that the kids and I could not completely despise her. For example, the midwife herself gave birth numerous times, but her babies all died. The midwife also, in spite of being coarse and arrogant, is wise, and she mentions as-a-matter-of-factly that a midwife will never walk out on the job. <br /><br />I had never thought about a midwife walking out on the job before, probably because it never happens. I have, however, witnessed doctors get so frustrated with patients that they walk out of the room. In fact, when I was giving birth to Fern, the doctor got so fed up with me for not wanting to speed up the labor, he actually walked out in a huff. A few minutes later, a midwife appeared. <br /><br />Her name was Vicki and she was chewing gum. She took one look at me and said, "Open your doors, Constance." After she checked me, she said, "I think you'll be more comfortable if you get on all fours." I was and five minutes later, Fern was born. Thank you, gum chewing midwife named Vicki! <br /><br />My point is this: Vicki's coarseness with me combined with her corny "Open your doors, Constance" command was exactly what was needed to get Fern out. No drugs involved. One of the tactics the midwife in Cushman's novel used was shouting the following into the birth canal:<br /><br />"Child come out! The light of Christ compels you!" <br /><br />I must admit I kind of like that!<br /><br />Midwifes are a huge asset to the health community and I wonder why there isn't a "midwife" for every field of health. <br /><br />This book is supposed to be about Alyce, the midwife's apprentice, but I spent more time concentrating on why the midwife and all the adults were so coarse and so ridiculously over-prepared for everything. I am naturally opposed to coarse behavior and over-preparing, so this book helped me understand why others are different. It also motivated me to tighten up a couple of my personal policies. <br /><br />I was happy when Alyce was recognized for her talent and I loved all of the birth stories (including the animals) as well as the medicinal and folk lore. We all especially loved the message about not quitting. My kids loved it and Jesse did, too, when he was home to listen. In other words, I recommend this book to everyone.<br /><br />Signed,<br />Don't Chew Gum at Work!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4212920519160815387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Emilie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187592-emilie"><img alt="Emilie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550984259p2/2187592.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127201078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16255402723517652101">There are few books that I come across, pick up, and just check out of the library on mere whim. There are even fewer books that I start over the minute I finish them.<br/>The Midwife's Apprentice is one of these precious few. <br/>It has no plot twits, mysteries, sexy vampires, gothic mansions, or pomp or circumstance. Its just a simple coming of age story about one of the sweetest, quietest, and purest characters to ever touch your soul. <br/>Its a short simple story, but its simplicity makes it so strong an</span>
  <span id="freeText16255402723517652101" style="display:none">There are few books that I come across, pick up, and just check out of the library on mere whim. There are even fewer books that I start over the minute I finish them.<br />The Midwife's Apprentice is one of these precious few. <br />It has no plot twits, mysteries, sexy vampires, gothic mansions, or pomp or circumstance. Its just a simple coming of age story about one of the sweetest, quietest, and purest characters to ever touch your soul. <br />Its a short simple story, but its simplicity makes it so strong and powerful. Its characters a rich and believable, its setting is described enough to where we get a general picture but can still imagine the rest for ourselves, and the story is so sweet and clear. I highly recommend it. It makes for great light reading and is an escape from all the heavy gothic and vampire romance out today. <br />its awesome and so wonderful. read it. Read it now!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2271867234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12198630961354648203">Saw this book listed on the audio list for the public library. Not necessarily a child's book, but closer to a young teen. Or for an old lady like me!<br/>Enjoying it as MY cat is curled up beside me. Interesting perspective of a homeless, poor girl who has never known her roots. She usually goes hungry. Sleeps burrowed into the warmth of a dung heap (if lucky to find one). At this point in the story (Chapter 7) her struggles are continuing, but she has been given some hope-chores for the mid-wife in</span>
  <span id="freeText12198630961354648203" style="display:none">Saw this book listed on the audio list for the public library. Not necessarily a child's book, but closer to a young teen. Or for an old lady like me!<br />Enjoying it as MY cat is curled up beside me. Interesting perspective of a homeless, poor girl who has never known her roots. She usually goes hungry. Sleeps burrowed into the warmth of a dung heap (if lucky to find one). At this point in the story (Chapter 7) her struggles are continuing, but she has been given some hope-chores for the mid-wife in return for scraps of bread or cheese. Which bless her, she's sharing with a stray cat that is hovering around, and has given her someone to talk to. <br />Ok. Back to the story...<br />Good little book. At first I didn't like the way (Alice as she named herself), kept putting herself down by repeatedly saying she was too stupid, but her thinking thankfully changed. By the book's end she had learned so much about herself and was selflessly aiding others. Her strengths and convictions surfaced, and she finally knew what she wanted to do with her life.</span>

<div id="review_513104573" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513104573" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1008175-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370231937p2/1008175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513104573?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/1008175-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1008175-kat?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1008175-kat?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1008175-kat?shelf=chapter-books-kids-and-tweens">chapter-books-kids-and-tweens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513104573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2705123093201039857">Basic Plot: A homeless girl in medieval England finds her place in the world and her purpose.<br/><br/>The situation of the poor girl at the beginning of the book about tore my heart out. Homeless children are a particularly hard thing for a parent to bear. This story was simple, but the meaning of it is what is really important. Alyce (the name she chooses for herself, as she had none at the beginning) really has nothing, not even pride, at the beginning of the story. She is abused by everyone around her</span>
  <span id="freeText2705123093201039857" style="display:none">Basic Plot: A homeless girl in medieval England finds her place in the world and her purpose.<br /><br />The situation of the poor girl at the beginning of the book about tore my heart out. Homeless children are a particularly hard thing for a parent to bear. This story was simple, but the meaning of it is what is really important. Alyce (the name she chooses for herself, as she had none at the beginning) really has nothing, not even pride, at the beginning of the story. She is abused by everyone around her because of her situation, until the local midwife offers her food in exchange for work. She becomes the midwife's apprentice and endures. Now, as I said, it's the message that's important. The only reason Alyce survives is because she KEEPS TRYING. In spite of her terrible situation she never gives up and she always keeps going. The midwife says she needs someone who "can do what I tell her, take what I give her, who can try and risk and fail and try again and not give up." So much in life depends on sheer, stubborn persistence that this is a vital lesson for anyone to learn. That this book teaches it to young people is valuable.<br /><br />I highly recommend it for any child of this age struggling with the idea of trying and failing. Failure is how we learn, so it's something we all must experience. It isn't fun, but it's very important. We have to remember that most of the time we can fix our mistakes and keep going, but not if we let ourselves get shut down by our failures.<br /><br />A vital lesson.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2705123093201039857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065865174" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer482158672570893119">I don't know how I remained ignorant of this book's existence for so longâ€”I read <i>Catherine, Called Birdy</i> growing up and felt like I encountered it fairly regularly in bookstores/libraries/other people's reading histories. When I did finally learn of <i>The Midwife's Apprentice</i> through GR, I was shocked that it actually has <i>more</i> ratings than CCB, and <i>won</i> the Newbury (which CCB was "only" nominated for). It kind of feels like I grew up a fan of Jamie Lynn Spears, thinking she was a big star, only to </span>
  <span id="freeText482158672570893119" style="display:none">I don't know how I remained ignorant of this book's existence for so longâ€”I read <i>Catherine, Called Birdy</i> growing up and felt like I encountered it fairly regularly in bookstores/libraries/other people's reading histories. When I did finally learn of <i>The Midwife's Apprentice</i> through GR, I was shocked that it actually has <i>more</i> ratings than CCB, and <i>won</i> the Newbury (which CCB was "only" nominated for). It kind of feels like I grew up a fan of Jamie Lynn Spears, thinking she was a big star, only to learn that she has some sister named Britney at the ripe old age of 24.<br /><br />Based on my memories of CCB, I was also expecting a lot more humor from this book than I got. There's certainly wit in the narration, as well as a good number of funny moments, but I remember Birdy being hysterical, and this book clearly wasn't going for that. Still, by the back half I found that the characters had endeared themselves to me despite my doubts. Even though I didn't grow up with this story, it had the same <i>feeling</i> of many of the stories I <i>did</i> grow up with. Something about the style and the way the narrative progressed felt incredibly familiar, which made the experience of reading it oddly comforting. Having recently read a nonfiction book set in the 14th century, it was also nice to be able to slightly expand my perspective of that time period. And now I want to reread <i>Catherine, Called Birdy</i> and see if it's really as funny as I remember it!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3232688739" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1281441736481040932">This was such a pleasant surprise! Cushman's writing reminded me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1973.Tracy_Chevalier' title='Tracy Chevalier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tracy Chevalier</a>'s writing. (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2865.Girl_with_a_Pearl_Earring' title='Girl with a Pearl Earring by Tracy Chevalier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girl with a Pearl Earring</a> is one of the very best historical fiction books I've read!) She was able to make me feel as if I was right there with Beetle/Alyce. I could glean the details of life during this time period through the character's actions. So easy and yet revealing! And, I particularly could relate to Beetle/Alyce since he companion was a an orange cat (appropriately named Purr!), much like </span>
  <span id="freeText1281441736481040932" style="display:none">This was such a pleasant surprise! Cushman's writing reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1973.Tracy_Chevalier" title="Tracy Chevalier" rel="nofollow noopener">Tracy Chevalier</a>'s writing. (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2865.Girl_with_a_Pearl_Earring" title="Girl with a Pearl Earring by Tracy Chevalier" rel="nofollow noopener">Girl with a Pearl Earring</a> is one of the very best historical fiction books I've read!) She was able to make me feel as if I was right there with Beetle/Alyce. I could glean the details of life during this time period through the character's actions. So easy and yet revealing! And, I particularly could relate to Beetle/Alyce since he companion was a an orange cat (appropriately named Purr!), much like my own "Big Boy" whom I rescued from our heating duct work on the morning after Christmas 2019! <br /><br />I doubt any of us can even imagine a child being totally abandoned and force to forage and steal for themselves just to live. But Beetle/Alyce makes her own way, regardless of the fact that she has no idea of her heritage, even her own birthday, or a name... Proof of the indomitable human spirit to survive and thrive!</span>

    <a title="Blake Medford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12120048-blake-medford"><img alt="Blake Medford" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13269894657663909312">I think that The Midwifeâ€™s Apprentice would be a book that would be difficult to teach in a middle grades setting.   <span id="freeText13269894657663909312" style="display:none">I think that The Midwifeâ€™s Apprentice would be a book that would be difficult to teach in a middle grades setting. The book covers how children are born and has some rather crude scenes. That being said I think to teach the book would depend on the area. An area that I wouldnâ€™t touch this book would be here in Georgia. In the middle of the Bible belt does not seem like the place to study a book that involves a woman yelling into another womenâ€™s vagina at a baby to come out. Considering how most the general consensus for the south to my knowledge is to keep sex a hidden topic just puts bad ideas of parents handling the book the wrong way. <br />	If I was going to teach the book though I would cover the main theme of the book and not go into much details of how children are born. That just seems like a terrible idea. The book would be alright to teach in an English class and I think that it could be used in a history class since it gives examples of how the world was back in the times when the world was still not as complex. It would be a great book for someone who is struggling in a class I think. If they could get the idea in their heads that giving up is not what they should do and instead they should struggle and do their best I think the world would be a lot better for it. Showing the students that taking the easy way out is not always the best idea and that in fact working hard to achieve a goal is something that should be encouraged.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText12337837752241399409" style="display:none">The story opens with a young girl with no name, no family, burying herself in a dung heap for warmth. The girl is taken in by a midwife, Jane, who dubs her Beetle for her choice of sleeping quarters. Janeâ€™s decision to take Beetle in is not due to benevolence, however, but greed; Jane sees that Beetle is a hard worker who will lighten her load. Jane gives Beetle all the difficult work of her profession, but she is careful to keep Beetle away from observing Jane during delivery, fearing Beetle will learn the secrets of midwifery and become a competitor.<br /><br />Slowly Beetle grows in experience and self-confidence, saving a boy from drowning, aiding a cow in delivering twins, even helping a mother with an impossible delivery give birth to a healthy girl. Beetle renames herself Alyce and she begins to learn Janeâ€™s secrets and aid Jane in deliveries.<br /><br />Then Alyce is confronted with a tough delivery. She finds she must call Jane in to save the mother and child. Alyce is left feeling despondent, useless. She runs away. <br /><br />It is only after much reflection that she is able to acknowledge her love for midwifery and to accept that failure is part of learning and to return to her work with Jane.<br /><br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer378949444" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6573504661218481305">How do you know when a piece of historical fiction is written really, really well? When the thought of living during that time makes you run for the shower! <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9640.Karen_Cushman' title='Karen Cushman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karen Cushman</a> has a gift for portraying time periods accurately, and the setting for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15595.The_Midwife_s_Apprentice' title='The Midwife's Apprentice by Karen Cushman' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Midwife's Apprentice</a> is no exception. As Beetle becomes more knowlegeable about her t</span>
  <span id="freeText6573504661218481305" style="display:none">How do you know when a piece of historical fiction is written really, really well? When the thought of living during that time makes you run for the shower! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9640.Karen_Cushman" title="Karen Cushman" rel="nofollow noopener">Karen Cushman</a> has a gift for portraying time periods accurately, and the setting for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15595.The_Midwife_s_Apprentice" title="The Midwife's Apprentice by Karen Cushman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midwife's Apprentice</a> is no exception. Beetle, our protagonist, is first described as sleeping in a dung pile, but is soon discovered by Jane, the curmudgeonly midwife who sets her to work as her apprentice. As Beetle becomes more knowlegeable about her trade, and even chooses her own name, she must learn how to make her own place in the world. Very well written, with vivid (no-holds-barred) description, this book pulls you back to the fourteenth century and at the end, while you'll be sad to see Beetle go, you'll be even more glad for running water and refrigerators!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349891579?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jess" href="/user/show/670054-jess">jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=zines">zines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=yaf">yaf</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349891579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14350951241704887715">I picked this up because I was fascinated to read about how midwifery was handled for a juvenile audience. You know how people freak out about kids knowing where babies come from? It was interesting from that perspective, but I ended up really enjoying the book. The protagonist is a homeless, nameless ragamuffin who gets taken in by a village midwife and learns a bit about the work of bringing babies into the world. The confidence that comes from having a place in the world starts to change the </span>
  <span id="freeText14350951241704887715" style="display:none">I picked this up because I was fascinated to read about how midwifery was handled for a juvenile audience. You know how people freak out about kids knowing where babies come from? It was interesting from that perspective, but I ended up really enjoying the book. The protagonist is a homeless, nameless ragamuffin who gets taken in by a village midwife and learns a bit about the work of bringing babies into the world. The confidence that comes from having a place in the world starts to change the girl. She gives herself a name, builds a family of sorts, overcomes some frightening challenges and develops into a capable, independent person. Without being too moralistic, this was a real "can do" story. I enjoyed it so much. I especially loved that the cat was a main character. Sometimes your cat is your only friend! That's real! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14350951241704887715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer764178109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15835314946742243965">This is a realistic medieval fiction for young readers 12+ and a well-deserved Newberry Medal winner. <br/><br/>This tale follows the trials and tribulations of a young girl (Beetle, named because as homeless she uses the dung for heat.) in early medieval times. She finds herself apprenticed to the local midwife, knowledge and wisdom alone, and finds her place in the world.<br/><br/>Cushman has researched the subject well. We learn about village life, medicine, feudal structure, and the place of women in that socie</span>
  <span id="freeText15835314946742243965" style="display:none">This is a realistic medieval fiction for young readers 12+ and a well-deserved Newberry Medal winner. <br /><br />This tale follows the trials and tribulations of a young girl (Beetle, named because as homeless she uses the dung for heat.) in early medieval times. She finds herself apprenticed to the local midwife, knowledge and wisdom alone, and finds her place in the world.<br /><br />Cushman has researched the subject well. We learn about village life, medicine, feudal structure, and the place of women in that society. <br /><br />This has few incidents which makes it, perhaps not the best book for much younger kids. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The near rape of Beetle by drunken boys, the midwife's affair with the baker, the well described birth scenes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But it's an important book worth remembering. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15835314946742243965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3231431814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16704090728310503059">This is not a book for young children, there are some serious issues and situations that this young lady experiences but I do believe that it showcases medieval village life as well as a short novel can. I was sad for this one to end, I really wanted to continue to follow Alyce's life now that she has finally found herself and the confidence she needs to really carve out a life for herself as a true midwife. If your child reads this, you will want to become familiar with it yourself as there are</span>
  <span id="freeText16704090728310503059" style="display:none">This is not a book for young children, there are some serious issues and situations that this young lady experiences but I do believe that it showcases medieval village life as well as a short novel can. I was sad for this one to end, I really wanted to continue to follow Alyce's life now that she has finally found herself and the confidence she needs to really carve out a life for herself as a true midwife. If your child reads this, you will want to become familiar with it yourself as there are some adult themes here and some practices that seem really strange with what we now know in modern times with modern medicine. There are many great discussion points to expand on here. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16704090728310503059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10933795876713426933">A young girl, on her own, finds the warmest spot to sleep in. One night she discovers the warmth of a dung heap and never leaves. She is discovered one day by Jane, the village midwife. Jane names her Beetle and takes her home to become an apprentice midwife. The girl hears the name Alyce one day and decides that she loves the name. And so she becomes Alyce. The midwife treats Alyce appallingly, but having nowhere to go, Alyce remains.<br/><br/>One night Alyce assists in a birth while the midwife assists </span>
  <span id="freeText10933795876713426933" style="display:none">A young girl, on her own, finds the warmest spot to sleep in. One night she discovers the warmth of a dung heap and never leaves. She is discovered one day by Jane, the village midwife. Jane names her Beetle and takes her home to become an apprentice midwife. The girl hears the name Alyce one day and decides that she loves the name. And so she becomes Alyce. The midwife treats Alyce appallingly, but having nowhere to go, Alyce remains.<br /><br />One night Alyce assists in a birth while the midwife assists another. Alyce is at a loss of what to do as the mother labors. She tries the things she's seen the midwife do but to no avail. The midwife herself finally returns and is able to deliver the child. Alyce believes she has no talents and runs away.<br /><br />She finds herself at an inn where she is able to be useful. But when a gaggle of strangers shows up one night and it is decided that the woman of the group is in labor, Alyce hides under the stairs. She wants no part of the goings-on. When everyone leaves the room, unable to deal with the laboring woman Alyce feels sympathy for her. She comes out of hiding and tries her best. And that's all it takes. After some hard work on the parts of both her and the mother, a little boy is born.<br /><br />Having gained her confidence Alyce returns to the midwife to finish her training. There's a place in the world for her after all.</span>

  <span id="freeText11929131636383211461" style="display:none">I read this aloud to my seven-year-olds. It held their attention most of the time, but they didnâ€™t beg me to read it to them like they did with the last book. I thought it was an okay book. The writing was good and I liked the light it shed on medieval English midwives (it doesnâ€™t go into a lot of detail, but what it did discuss seemed well-researched). There werenâ€™t many swear words, and most of them wouldnâ€™t have bothered me in a book for adults or teenagers, but this was a middle grade book, so I was hoping for squeaky-clean. All in all, not a bad book, but not one Iâ€™m dying to recommend to everyone.</span>

<div id="review_1287007770" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1287007770" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1287007770?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13333393-the-midwife-s-apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=newbery-medal-and-honor">newbery-medal-and-honor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287007770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6219922169561880337">Beautifully told historical fiction for Middle School students. Set in Medieval England, it tells the story of a young girl searching for identity. The story highlights how identity is shaped both by our own understanding of self and the outer world's perception of what we are, how it shifts and grows along with our experiences. The main character's name is a wonderful symbol for this development. First, the young orphan is only known as Brat, later she is called Beetle. In the end, she gives he</span>
  <span id="freeText6219922169561880337" style="display:none">Beautifully told historical fiction for Middle School students. Set in Medieval England, it tells the story of a young girl searching for identity. The story highlights how identity is shaped both by our own understanding of self and the outer world's perception of what we are, how it shifts and grows along with our experiences. The main character's name is a wonderful symbol for this development. First, the young orphan is only known as Brat, later she is called Beetle. In the end, she gives herself a name and thereby chooses an identity for herself - Alyce. Alyce turns into an active creator of identity when she helps a little boy find a name and a place for himself in the world.<br />The story is also about resilience and learning how to face failure and go on trying. It is about understanding that life is not a fairytale, but that you can actively change it for the better if you are brave enough to stand up for yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6219922169561880337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('irlWeagf7FIiyKT/psjNgWL9XuGZDILFBstzl83Nyp0HGGYJLLwrgfNaM1m1wwEBG2hazcmvfM6R9hNlaZ/FUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TML6R4+YoXuxClLK9jNjcTwHX5hAmeXSMkjh232ISD/BY8o3CztmqGCYxWzlOK/xRZJbtBA6G9mldYEp2dpH8A==')})
  }

  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
